<div id="review_88532579" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/88532579" />
    <a title="Christina " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2621042-christina"><img alt="Christina " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1302034398p2/2621042.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/88532579?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina " href="/user/show/2621042-christina">Christina </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2621042-christina?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer88532579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10223482408868543990">Okay, so this book surprised me and I didn't see it coming.<br/><br/>Firstly because ever since I heard that Mencheres was getting a book, I was never <i>overly</i> interested in his story. I mean, I liked his character, sure, but a whole book about him? Meh. And then I read the first Night Huntress World novel, (Spade's story) and was more than a little put off. Very generic pnr, the hero was boring and unoriginal, whilst the heroine was truly bang-your-head-against-the-wall annoying.<br/><br/>Anyway, I started reading E</span>
  <span id="freeText10223482408868543990" style="display:none">Okay, so this book surprised me and I didn't see it coming.<br /><br />Firstly because ever since I heard that Mencheres was getting a book, I was never <i>overly</i> interested in his story. I mean, I liked his character, sure, but a whole book about him? Meh. And then I read the first Night Huntress World novel, (Spade's story) and was more than a little put off. Very generic pnr, the hero was boring and unoriginal, whilst the heroine was truly bang-your-head-against-the-wall annoying.<br /><br />Anyway, I started reading EKoD with a great deal of skepticism. I should also say that I don't read much paranormal romance, but I prefered Frost's books because I'm already familiar with her characters so some of their growth and analysis have already been accomplished in the previous books. It's easier to relate, easier to understand.<br /><br />Mencheres is propably my favorite character now, (after Vlad of course). In the Cat and Bones books, he was a cool and somewhat detached character, and seemed pretty stereotypical. A father figure to the hero, very utilitarian , often a way to progress the story and divulge worldbuilding information.<br /> <br />Astonishingly, EKoD's Mencheres is a strong,self-deprecating, funny, earthily sexy man, whose way of thinking and actions come across as both legitimate and sincere. His exchanges with Kira were intermittently funny, hot and sweet.<br /><br />In many pnr books(both adult and ya) what bothers me is exactly this: how the old,savvy and jaded immortal protagonist is magically swept off his feet by the mortal he loves(see:lusts for)and everything about his character and way of life changes. We are practically slapped with a makeover and a HEA with no further development. <br /><br />But here the progress is slow(er) and believable, and there is no drastic character rewrite or sugarcoating. Mencheres retains his good and bad attributes and so does the heroine. The couple's HEA is not their sins atoned, but the fact that they simply come together. I also appreciated the fact that Frost decided to build their relationship not on lust-on-sight but on a sense of deeper connection. I'm propably not conveying this well, but their progress felt more humane, realistic, satisfying than others. They are similar, kindred souls, and they, quite simply, recognize it.<br /><br />As for the heroine, Kira, I loved her. She was smart, spunky and brave, loving and generous. The absolute opposite of TSTL. Her sincerity about her feelings, and aknowledgement of her faults is remarkable. (Denise, eat your heart out). Her objections and reactions were realistic and never overexaggerating. What won me over was the fact that she didn't beat around the bush about her nature,her feelings. Attagirl.<br /><br />There is an appearence from Vlad!! Damn, I love his portrayal, a mixture of brutal honesty, sarcastic humor and heartbreaking insights into his soul. Frost is planning a new series about him, not just a NHW book. <br /><br />That said, EKoD could have used a few more pages and the protagonists did come together a little too fast for my liking. But as I said, I at least, was, in the end, satisfied about their development. It was honest.<br /><br />Liked this one a great deal, as you can tell by my wildly incoherent rant that's supposed to pass as a review, but oh well. ;)<br /><br />*3,5 stars.<br /><br />P.S.:Kinky ceiling sex. If that's not going to persuade you, I don't know what is. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10223482408868543990" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_450007952" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/450007952" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14323468-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434090906p2/14323468.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/450007952?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/14323468-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=gr2015">gr2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=i-want">i-want</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer450007952" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18022754027620471072"><p>I have to admit, I was never really interested in Mencheres before. Honestly, he came across as OLD, and unsexy. But I’m so glad that Jeaniene Frost proved me wrong.</p> <p> Mencheres is tired, alone and weighted down with guilt. Mostly everyone in his life, especially women, has only been attracted to him because of his power or his wealth. No one has ever done anything for him in exchange for nothing. There has always been ulterior motives. Until now….</p> <p>In order to stop his long-time nemesis from obta</p></span>
  <span id="freeText18022754027620471072" style="display:none"><p>I have to admit, I was never really interested in Mencheres before. Honestly, he came across as OLD, and unsexy. But I’m so glad that Jeaniene Frost proved me wrong.</p> <p> Mencheres is tired, alone and weighted down with guilt. Mostly everyone in his life, especially women, has only been attracted to him because of his power or his wealth. No one has ever done anything for him in exchange for nothing. There has always been ulterior motives. Until now….</p> <p>In order to stop his long-time nemesis from obtaining his power, he has decided that he has to die. Also, he has lost his visions, and see only darkness, believing therefor that death is coming for him. While waiting for ghouls to finish him off, he is saved by P.I. Kira Graceling, a human who has no idea that supernatural exists, and only wants to save the man who is being tortured. But while trying to save Mencheres, Kira is mortally wounded, and Mencheres has to heal her. But because he is unable to hypnotize her into forgetting about him and what happended, he kidnaps her, so that he can try again after a few days.</p> <p>I really enjoyed the chemistry between Mencheres and Kira. And I loved how determined Kira was at first to get away from Mencheres. Kira is definitely not meek, she has so much courage, even when she’s afraid, and she had no problem putting Mencheres in his place. It was hilarious seeing Mecheres react to the first person in perhaps ever telling him no, and refusing to listen to him. Their relationship was slow building, even though the attraction was instant, because neither wanted to admit to their feelings. And because Mencheres doesn’t want to risk Kira’s life, even though he can’t stop thinking about her, he lets her go. But of course fate intervenes, and brings them into contact again. And so their journey to their HEA continues.</p> <p>I loved how Kira saw Mencheres, and she definitely brought out his sexy side ;-). She also brought back beauty and love into his life, and gave him motivation in fighting to live. They were just perfect for each other. </p> <p>Of course, almost all my favorite characters made appearances, and I really enjoyed Vlad’s snarky attitude, as I always do :-).</p> <blockquote>“Mencheres,” the stranger said. “If anyone other than you had me fly halfway around the world just to keep me waiting while you were obviously lingering in bed, I’d have my driver run them over. Twice.”</blockquote> <p>A really enjoyable addition to this series, and a must read for all lovers of the Night Huntress World. </p></span>
  <a data-text-id="18022754027620471072" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_111504238" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/111504238" />
    <a title="Quinn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2310262-quinn"><img alt="Quinn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1300839213p2/2310262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/111504238?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Quinn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Quinn" href="/user/show/2310262-quinn">Quinn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2310262-quinn?shelf=library-book">library-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2310262-quinn?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2310262-quinn?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer111504238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4643722427571837836"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>I am very pleasantly surprised by how much I enjoyed this book. There are a couple of reasons for this:<br/><br/>First and foremost, Mencheres had never struck me as having any obvious potential as a romantic, sexy hero. Sure, he was interesting in an ancient and powerful way, but without any sex appeal to speak of.<br/><br/>Secondly, I was slightly spoiled by reading this one out of order – and don’t get me started on the whole issue of a spin-off series not being a spin-off in anything but name. You can </span>
  <span id="freeText4643722427571837836" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br /><br />I am very pleasantly surprised by how much I enjoyed this book. There are a couple of reasons for this:<br /><br />First and foremost, Mencheres had never struck me as having any obvious potential as a romantic, sexy hero. Sure, he was interesting in an ancient and powerful way, but without any sex appeal to speak of.<br /><br />Secondly, I was slightly spoiled by reading this one out of order – and don’t get me started on the whole issue of a spin-off series not being a spin-off in anything but name. You can and will spoil both series (<i>Night Huntress</i> and <i>Night Huntress World</i>) if you don’t read them strictly in order. Ugh. I can feel another major rant coming on, and even though it is well deserved, you can just refer to <a>my review</a> of <i>This Side of the Grave</i>. Suffice it to say, I am still really aggravated about this.<br /><br />Argh. Now I’m going to have to walk away for a while so I’m capable of doing something other than ranting about the cross-over between the series’ and the fact that the author forces you to read both in order to know what’s going on in either one. See? I can’t help it. My fingers are aching to type a major rant. Must. Not. Go. There.<br /><br />Back to my first point. Mencheres was indeed a worthy hero. I saw him in such a different light in this book, and without the author needing to make drastic changes to his character. He was still the powerful, formal, reserved vampire I was used to, but getting to see inside his head and learn about his past made a significant difference.<br /><br />But not as much as seeing him fall for Kira. And I could totally see why he did. I think Kira is the most appealing heroine Frost has written yet – and I do include Cat in that statement. Kira was everything a heroine should be and then some. I loved the way she was prepared to fight for Mencheres (both figuratively and literally), and I loved seeing her stand her ground on the strength of her convictions. <br /><br />I seldom have much to say about the heroines in the books I read – I’m all about the heroes! – but Kira is definitely worth appreciating. I wish there were more heroines like her - she's one of the best I've ever read in PNR/UF. I’m really hoping she plays a big role in future books, because I didn’t appreciate her in <i>This Side of the Grave</i>, not having read this one first.<br /><br />See what I mean about the freaking order you have to read these in? Gah.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4643722427571837836" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_88450524" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/88450524" />
    <a title="AH" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3255548-ah"><img alt="AH" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1275413869p2/3255548.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/88450524?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AH" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AH" href="/user/show/3255548-ah">AH</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3255548-ah?shelf=zzread-feb2011">zzread-feb2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer88450524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13158338401414576284">3.5 stars<br/><br/>It was with anticipation that I picked up Eternal Kiss of Darkness. I enjoy Jeaniene Frost’s books and I was looking forward to Mencheres’ story. After all, Mencheres is such a powerful vampire and his story had to be great.<br/><br/>Unfortunately, Mencheres’ character fell a little flat for me. For a master vampire, I was expecting a lot of “special talents.” Mencheres seemed a little mopey and self destructive until….the lovely Kira Graceling falls into his life. Kira saved the story for me. It</span>
  <span id="freeText13158338401414576284" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br />It was with anticipation that I picked up Eternal Kiss of Darkness. I enjoy Jeaniene Frost’s books and I was looking forward to Mencheres’ story. After all, Mencheres is such a powerful vampire and his story had to be great.<br /><br />Unfortunately, Mencheres’ character fell a little flat for me. For a master vampire, I was expecting a lot of “special talents.” Mencheres seemed a little mopey and self destructive until….the lovely Kira Graceling falls into his life. Kira saved the story for me. It is refreshing to see a strong female character for a change. Kira has confidence in Mencheres and suddenly he is obsessed with her safety and well being. Kira is also exceptionally strong as a newly made vampire.<br /><br />I was very happy when Bones and Vlad stepped into the story. They made the story for me. I especially appreciate Vlad’s character and I hope that there is a book planned for him in the future. Vlad’s story should be very interesting. <br /><br />I found the villain Rajedef a little irksome. Yes, he was power hungry and evil. But he was mostly annoying. <br /><br />Despite its few flaws, Eternal Kiss of Darkness was an enjoyable read. The pacing was good and there was a lot of excitement towards the end. I loved learning about Mencheres’ back story. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13158338401414576284" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_538358430" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/538358430" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1376766-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582132250p2/1376766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/538358430?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/1376766-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=ebook_nook">ebook_nook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=mystery-and-thrillers">mystery-and-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=romance-y">romance-y</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer538358430" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3315538383543631834">I'm actually really surprised by my rating for this one. I enjoyed it quite a bit, despite - or possibly because of - Mencheres being one of my least favorite characters from the NH series. I didn't really cut him any slack here; hot sex or no, I wanted a decent story...and there WAS hot sex. My goodness, it made Spade and Denise from the last NHW book look like they were awkward gropey teens... and that's just not sexy at all.<br/><br/>Mencheres... well... I may not give up my preference for Bones... but</span>
  <span id="freeText3315538383543631834" style="display:none">I'm actually really surprised by my rating for this one. I enjoyed it quite a bit, despite - or possibly because of - Mencheres being one of my least favorite characters from the NH series. I didn't really cut him any slack here; hot sex or no, I wanted a decent story...and there WAS hot sex. My goodness, it made Spade and Denise from the last NHW book look like they were awkward gropey teens... and that's just not sexy at all.<br /><br />Mencheres... well... I may not give up my preference for Bones... but one could do a lot worse than to read about Menchere's naughties. He's GOOD at them. <br /><br />And on top of that, I actually came to kinda like him toward the end. I realize now that what I didn't like about him before was his monotone aloofness. He's the all-knowing, wise, father-figure who shows up to provide strength, but doesn't really do much else but brood a lot. And for a goodish chunk of this book, he continued on that road... but Kira brought out a new side of him... a lighter side. And I LIKED it. I like seeing Mencheres laugh and tease and enjoy himself. <br /><br />And I liked that there was no fucking instalove. YYYYYAAAAAAAYYYY!!!! <br />\(O_O)/<br /><br />Kira and Mencheres didn't just see each other and fall head over heels in lust-I-mean-love - they actually formed a kind of relationship and interest in each other before that. There was a progression of attraction and liking and interest! It actually took me a while to recognize why I was feeling like this was just a better book than FDOC - but toward the end, around the time that Kira realized the significance of the situation in which she met Mencheres, I realized that there's just been this growing connection between them that actually consisted of something more than just saying that there was one. <br /><br />They have things in common. They have similar pasts (though, admittedly, one's is much more vast than the other's), and similar betrayal experiences, and similar consciousness of the powerless people who could be hurt by their actions... or inaction. There's a base of commonality that their relationship stood on, and I really liked that a lot. <br /><br />Kira, also, was no moronic girl who couldn't be trusted to tie her own shoes without a man guiding her. I liked her a LOT. She has personality, and spunk, and her own will and damn the consequences. And when those consequences actually bite her in the ass, she doesn't back down or run away or whine or cry about it, but stands her ground and holds her head up, because she is willing to take the responsibility for herself. So good. <br /><br />I do feel like I would have liked more closure with Tina though - just a quick follow-up meeting with her after everything, to meet the boyfriend as promised. See how she's coping with her new knowledge and family and whatnot. <br /><br />And I do feel like the resolution was just a little rushed - but still enjoyable. <br /><br />Definitely much better than I expected for this one to be, and I'd recommend this one over First Drop of Crimson any day. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3315538383543631834" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_740469413" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/740469413" />
    <a title="Maria Dimitrova" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15922517-maria-dimitrova"><img alt="Maria Dimitrova" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563534668p2/15922517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/740469413?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria Dimitrova" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria Dimitrova" href="/user/show/15922517-maria-dimitrova">Maria Dimitrova</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15922517-maria-dimitrova?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15922517-maria-dimitrova?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15922517-maria-dimitrova?shelf=br-bbb-2019">br-bbb-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer740469413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10586515933073020349"><b>Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/27962805-choko' rel='nofollow noopener'>Choko</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four' rel='nofollow noopener'>Robin</a>.</b><br/><br/>Up until this moment Mencheres was this aloof, mysterious puppet-master that was technically on Cat and Bones' side. The thing is he was hardly a character you could root for. Sympathize a little with but never really identify with. <i>Eternal Kiss of Darkness</i> changes that.<br/><br/>We start this with a suicidal but determined to protect his line at all costs Mencheres and a human girl who gets involved in the preternatural because of her inability to ignore someone in trouble</span>
  <span id="freeText10586515933073020349" style="display:none"><b>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/27962805-choko" rel="nofollow noopener">Choko</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four" rel="nofollow noopener">Robin</a>.</b><br /><br />Up until this moment Mencheres was this aloof, mysterious puppet-master that was technically on Cat and Bones' side. The thing is he was hardly a character you could root for. Sympathize a little with but never really identify with. <i>Eternal Kiss of Darkness</i> changes that.<br /><br />We start this with a suicidal but determined to protect his line at all costs Mencheres and a human girl who gets involved in the preternatural because of her inability to ignore someone in trouble. I loved Kira from the get go because of that. It's a rare thing in today's society where a lot of people will see that you need help and just walk by. And on the next day when they watch the news and see that something terrible has happened they won't even remember that they've been in a position to help. <br /><br />I loved that we got to learn more about Mencheres and what his life was like both as a pharaoh and then as one of the oldest vampires in existence. Seeing him struggling with life without his visions and the insecurity that it caused in this otherwise very confident character was eye-opening. and while it made my sympathize with him more I also felt like he deserved to be put in that situation to see how it feels to be the pawn instead of the puppet-master.<br /><br />When I first read this book about 5 years ago I felt like the relationship between Kira and Mencheres was a bit rushed. Having the chance to re-read the events and with the help of a few more years of experience, I could see that this was not the case. Maybe the first time I was too focused on the plotline with Radjedef or maybe I just lacked the ability to see the little details back then, I will never know. But I'm glad I had the chance to re-experience things and think them over with better attention to the smaller things. It helped me appreciate both the book and the characters more.<br /><br />Talking about character appreciation, I was struck by how much I have ignored one of the recurring side characters. I should have known better since Veritas shows up a lot over the course of the series and with the events of this book some of what happens in the future shouldn't have come as such a surprise when it did. But of course I totally didn't pay attention to all the foreshadowing and little tidbits thrown here and there in the series. The mare fact that she shows up so often should have clued me in that Ms. Frost has plans for her. So if you're first time readers, I suggest you pay special attention to her and how she reacts to things. I promise it will be worth it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10586515933073020349" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1451439813" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1451439813" />
    <a title="CC" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25476191-cc"><img alt="CC" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1433519972p2/25476191.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1451439813?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="CC" class="user" itemprop="url" name="CC" href="/user/show/25476191-cc">CC</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8680662-eternal-kiss-of-darkness">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25476191-cc?shelf=safe-but-other-triggers">safe-but-other-triggers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25476191-cc?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25476191-cc?shelf=dead-ex-spouse">dead-ex-spouse</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1451439813" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16382974466948696093">I have no idea what to say about this book. I usually form an opinion immediately when reading or at least when I finish. I finished this last night and still have no idea what I really think about it so I will just give some technical comments.<br/><br/>It was a well written and well developed story. It was complex and I think readers who have read her previous series will be better prepared to jump into this vampire world but I was not totally lost not having read any prior books.<br/><br/>This is a darker vampir</span>
  <span id="freeText16382974466948696093" style="display:none">I have no idea what to say about this book. I usually form an opinion immediately when reading or at least when I finish. I finished this last night and still have no idea what I really think about it so I will just give some technical comments.<br /><br />It was a well written and well developed story. It was complex and I think readers who have read her previous series will be better prepared to jump into this vampire world but I was not totally lost not having read any prior books.<br /><br />This is a darker vampire world than I have read in more recent paranormal romance novels. Humans are "property". They can be killed, traded, used, etc. Feeding is a sensual experience whether it be men or women. <br /><br />There were items in this story that I do not prefer (dead exes) but it did not effect my enjoyment of the story. The Hero pushes her away - A LOT! If she was not so honest and forward, they would have never gotten together. It made me really love the heroine. She was brave and open with the Hero. I admired how accepting she was, her support of her sister, and her sticking up for the Hero many times. But honestly I am not really sure why she loved the Hero. He was not a bad guy - even though he kept saying he was. But he did zero to endear himself to her, constantly talked bad about himself, spent very little time with her (before they were together-together); so I just do not get it. <br /><br />In general I enjoyed the book, but something about this book just did not draw me in. I believe the issue was that I did not really love the Hero. I liked him and he got much better after the book got about half way through, but I was already detached by then. I am interested in Vlad's story but do not plan to read other books.<br /><br /> <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16382974466948696093" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <td colspan="2">

<span id="freeTextContainer11998251541555274636">Kira, a private investigator, ends up being unexpectedly thrown into Mencheres world. She's feisty, stubborn, intelligent, and loyal. It was odd to read about Mencheres because for some reason I always pictured him as being older. Not the young, vibrant man in the story. <br/>Mencheres has an ancient enemy who feels that he is entitled to Mencheres' powers. He's been waiting for millinnia to find a way to force the transfer of power. Now, Mencheres is showing emotions, and getting close to a female f</span>
  <span id="freeText11998251541555274636" style="display:none">Kira, a private investigator, ends up being unexpectedly thrown into Mencheres world. She's feisty, stubborn, intelligent, and loyal. It was odd to read about Mencheres because for some reason I always pictured him as being older. Not the young, vibrant man in the story. <br />Mencheres has an ancient enemy who feels that he is entitled to Mencheres' powers. He's been waiting for millinnia to find a way to force the transfer of power. Now, Mencheres is showing emotions, and getting close to a female for the first time in centuries. His rival feels that this is time to force Mencheres' hand, putting Kira in danger. <br />I enjoyed this one. It's not as "sexy" as the other ones, but it was cute. I really wish Mencheres was more of a tease (although I get why he isn't). That's why I love Bones so much. It's the banter back and forth before anyone jumps into bed that I love. It's the double entendres and witty little comments that make you blush.... Those are the moments I love. Mencheres is a little too much like Eeyore. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11998251541555274636" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

it's time to part, Kira is more disappointed than she expected, and when she realizes that Mencheres has not forgotten her as she believed, she uses her skills to find him.<br /><br />That's how she ends up in a very sticky situation, where the only good option is being turned into a vampire by Mencheres.<br /><br />Unfortunately, a power hungry old enemy is determined to get Mencheres's power just in time to save Kira and deal with his old enemy once and for all <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />An enjoyable story in the familiar Night Huntress universe, with a well suited couple that get a well deserved happily ever after.<br /><br />I read the books a bit out of order, but I am looking forward to Vlad's story next in <a <div id="review_94551331" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/94551331" />
    <a title="Alisha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1503257-alisha"><img alt="Alisha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305444015p2/1503257.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/94551331?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alisha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alisha" href="/user/show/1503257-alisha">Alisha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer94551331" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9167214238183526004"><b>Rating:4.5</b><br/>Okay, so…forget a summary. Let me start out by saying that I <i>loved</i> the heroine of this book, Kira Graceling. She's no-nonsense and smart, with a troubled past and tough life circumstances, but possessing a strong will to survive. Girlfriend rolls with the punches, but also fights for what she sees as just. She is introduced as a brand new character, notably amongst a bunch of people we already know well (and might even love ^_^). Yet she managed to be the one I connected to most. She t</span>
  <span id="freeText9167214238183526004" style="display:none"><b>Rating:4.5</b><br />Okay, so…forget a summary. Let me start out by saying that I <i>loved</i> the heroine of this book, Kira Graceling. She's no-nonsense and smart, with a troubled past and tough life circumstances, but possessing a strong will to survive. Girlfriend rolls with the punches, but also fights for what she sees as just. She is introduced as a brand new character, notably amongst a bunch of people we already know well (and might even love ^_^). Yet she managed to be the one I connected to most. She totally beats Cat and Denise for the spot of "awesomest Night Huntress/World Character." Yay, Kira!<br /><br />Now, as for the book itself. I have to say that I was not hooked from the get-go with this story. Some of the early interactions between Mencheres and Kira were a bit on the "been there, done that" side at times, feeling slightly predictable and underwhelming. However, as the story plowed on and the plot deepened, the addiction factor went up accordingly.<br /><br />As with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6547187.First_Drop_of_Crimson__Night_Huntress_World___1_" title="First Drop of Crimson (Night Huntress World, #1) by Jeaniene Frost" rel="nofollow noopener">First Drop of Crimson</a>, both Bones and Cat make guest appearances, and again I found them to be fairly subtle, not overdone. Didn't feel gimmicky, either. Of course, Bones' appearance in the story was a necessity due to his relationship to Mencheres, but still. I'm glad the B&amp;C train didn't stop in town for too long.<br /><br />IMO, a very satisfying entry to the PnR-based Night Huntress World series. Looking forward to the next entry (<i>please</i> let it be Vlad!)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9167214238183526004" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iE3QcwpvqlSaOHP+Ej9mb6r2RzO8SJf/TIrKN9rYaw6ya7mhsTFjPD0Tx5/lymywfKmg+3LFGZgX9IyGF5uZlA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SBchToYdEvxRbcN8IwFw/9DwaqAtmQfGhaNG1sBJesVyMUicPUPblPZGdx3U9HogBq+NaOMUiaHe3QBnDQqIXw==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer9698904430470843559">Jeaniene Frost is the New York Times, USA Today, and international bestselling author of the Night Huntress series, the Night Prince series, the Broken Destiny series, and the new Night Rebel series. To date, foreign rights for her novels have sold to twenty different countries. Jeaniene lives in Florida with her husband Matthew, who long ago accepted that she rarely cooks and always sleeps in on </span>
  <span id="freeText9698904430470843559" style="display:none">Jeaniene Frost is the New York Times, USA Today, and international bestselling author of the Night Huntress series, the Night Prince series, the Broken Destiny series, and the new Night Rebel series. To date, foreign rights for her novels have sold to twenty different countries. Jeaniene lives in Florida with her husband Matthew, who long ago accepted that she rarely cooks and always sleeps in on the weekends. Aside from writing, Jeaniene enjoys reading, poetry, watching movies with her husband, exploring old cemeteries, spelunking and traveling – by car. Airplanes, children, and cook books frighten her.<br /><br />For information on Jeaniene's books, book trailers, deleted scenes, creature mythology, and more, please visit: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jeanienefrost.com">www.jeanienefrost.com</a><br /></span>

Now her survival depends on an immortal who craves a taste of her.\n\nHe is Spade, a powerful, mysterious vampire who has walked the earth for centuries and is now duty-bound to protect this endangered, alluring human – even if it means destroying his own kind. Denise may arouse his deepest hungers, but Spade knows he must fight his urge to have her as they face the demon nightmare together…\n\nBecause once the first drop of crimson falls, they will both be
